	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Stephen Decatur</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Steven_Decatur&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Steven Decatur">Steven Decatur</a>)</span></div>
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">United States Navy officer</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other people named Stephen Decatur, see <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Stephen Decatur (disambiguation)">Stephen Decatur (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p><b>Stephen Decatur Jr.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>; January 5, 1779&#160;– March 22, 1820) was a United States naval officer and <a href="/wiki/Commodore_(rank)" title="Commodore (rank)">commodore</a>.  He was born on the eastern shore of <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Worcester_County,_Maryland" title="Worcester County, Maryland">Worcester County</a>, the son of a U.S. naval officer who served during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>. His father, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur_Sr." title="Stephen Decatur Sr.">Stephen Decatur Sr.</a>, was a commodore in the U.S. Navy, and brought the younger Stephen into the world of ships and sailing early on. Shortly after attending college, Decatur followed in his father's footsteps and joined the U.S. Navy at the age of nineteen as a <a href="/wiki/Midshipman" title="Midshipman">midshipman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur supervised the construction of several U.S. naval vessels, one of which he later commanded. Promoted at age 25, he is the youngest man to reach the rank of <a href="/wiki/Captain_(naval)" title="Captain (naval)">captain</a> in the history of the United States Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He served under three presidents, and played a major role in the early development of the American navy. In almost every theater of operation, Decatur's service was characterized by acts of heroism and exceptional performance. His service in the Navy took him through both <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Wars" title="Barbary Wars">Barbary Wars</a> in North Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Quasi-War" title="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</a> with France, and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> with Britain. He was renowned for his natural ability to lead and for his genuine concern for the <a href="/wiki/Sailor" title="Sailor">seamen</a> under his command.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> His numerous naval victories against Britain, France and the Barbary states established the United States Navy as a rising power.
</p><p>During this period he served aboard and commanded many naval vessels and ultimately became a member of the Board of Navy Commissioners. He built a large home in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Decatur_House" title="Decatur House">Decatur House</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Lafayette_Square_Historic_District,_Washington,_D.C." title="Lafayette Square Historic District, Washington, D.C.">Lafayette Square</a>, and was the center of Washington society in the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He became an affluent member of Washington society and counted <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a> and other Washington dignitaries among his personal friends.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur's career came to an early end when he was killed in a duel with Commodore <a href="/wiki/James_Barron" title="James Barron">James Barron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> They fought after he refused to retract remarks he had made about Barron's conduct in the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake%E2%80%93Leopard_affair" title="Chesapeake–Leopard affair">Chesapeake–Leopard affair</a> in 1807. Decatur emerged as a national hero in his own lifetime, becoming the first post-<a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">Revolutionary War</a> hero. His name and legacy, like that of <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones" title="John Paul Jones">John Paul Jones</a>, became identified with the United States Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Decatur was born on January 5, 1779 in <a href="/wiki/Sinepuxent,_Maryland" title="Sinepuxent, Maryland">Sinepuxent, Maryland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur_Sr." title="Stephen Decatur Sr.">Stephen Decatur Sr.</a>, a merchant captain and later an officer in the young American navy during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, and his wife Ann (Pine) Decatur. The family of Decatur was of French descent on Stephen's father's side, while his mother's family was of Irish ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> His parents had arrived from <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> just three months before Stephen was born, having to flee that city during the American Revolution because of the British occupation. They later returned to the same residence they had once left in Philadelphia<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  and Decatur grew up there, eventually graduating from the Episcopal Academy.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur came to love the sea and sailing in a roundabout manner. When Stephen was eight years old, he developed a severe case of <a href="/wiki/Whooping_cough" title="Whooping cough">whooping cough</a>. In those days, a supposed tonic for this condition was exposure to the salt air of the sea. It was decided that Stephen Jr. would accompany his father aboard a <a href="/wiki/Merchant_vessel" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant vessel">merchant ship</a> on his next voyage to Europe. Sailing across the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> and back proved to be an effective remedy, and Decatur came home completely recovered. In the days following young Stephen's return he was jubilant about his adventure on the high sea and spoke of wanting to go sailing often. His parents had different aspirations, especially his mother who had hopes that Stephen would one day become an <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal</a> clergyman, and tried to discourage the eight-year-old from such jaunty ambitions, fearing such would distract Stephen from his studies.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bradford_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradford-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur attended <a href="/wiki/Woodbury_Junior-Senior_High_School" title="Woodbury Junior-Senior High School">Woodbury Academy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Woodbury,_New_Jersey" title="Woodbury, New Jersey">Woodbury, New Jersey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> At the direction of his father, Decatur attended the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Academy" title="Episcopal Academy">Episcopal Academy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> at the time an all-boys school that specialized in Latin, mathematics and religion; however, Decatur had not applied himself adequately, and barely graduated from the academy. He then enrolled for one year at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a> in 1795,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> where he better applied himself and focused on his studies. At the university, Decatur met and became friends with <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_(1778%E2%80%931869)" title="Charles Stewart (1778–1869)">Charles Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Somers" title="Richard Somers">Richard Somers</a>, who would later become naval officers themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur found the <a href="/wiki/Classics" title="Classics">classic studies</a> prosaic and life at the university disagreeable, and at the age of 17, with his heart and mind set on ships and the sea, discontinued his studies there. Though his parents were not pleased with his decision, they were apparently wise enough to now let the aspiring young man pursue his own course through life.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis,_1937_p.7_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis,_1937_p.7-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Through his father's influence, Stephen gained employment at the shipbuilding firm of Gurney and Smith, business associates of his father, acting as supervisor to the early construction of the frigate <a href="/wiki/USS_United_States_(1797)" title="USS United States (1797)"><i>United States</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He was serving on board this vessel as a midshipman when it was launched on May 10, 1797,<sup id="cite_ref-bradford_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bradford-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> under the command of <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">Commodore John Barry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_2004,_pp.10-11_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_2004,_pp.10-11-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-commission">Pre-commission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-commission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the years leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Quasi-War" title="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</a>, an undeclared naval war with the revolutionary <a href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="First French Republic">French Republic</a> (<a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>) involving disputes over U.S. trading and shipping with Britain, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">U.S. Congress</a> passed the '<a href="/wiki/Naval_Act_of_1794" title="Naval Act of 1794">Act to provide for a Naval Armament</a>' on March 27, 1794. The act provided for the commissioning of <a href="/wiki/Original_six_frigates_of_the_United_States_Navy" title="Original six frigates of the United States Navy">six frigates</a> for the Navy. It was promptly signed by <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> that same day. There was much opposition to the bill, and it was amended and allowed to pass with the condition that work on the proposed ships would stop in the event that peace with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Algeria" title="Ottoman Algeria">Pasha of Algiers</a> was obtained.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>  Construction of the six new American <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> was progressing slowly when, because of a peace accord with Algiers in March 1796, work was halted. After some debate and at the insistence of President Washington, Congress passed an act on April 20, 1796, allowing the construction and funding to continue, but only on the three ships nearest to completion at the time: <a href="/wiki/USS_United_States_(1797)" title="USS United States (1797)">USS&#160;<i>United States</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Constellation_(1797)" title="USS Constellation (1797)">USS&#160;<i>Constellation</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Constitution" title="USS Constitution">USS&#160;<i>Constitution</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1798, <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">John Barry</a> obtained Decatur's appointment as midshipman on <i>United States</i>, under Barry's command. Barry was a veteran and hero of the Revolutionary War and was Decatur's good friend and mentor. Decatur accepted the appointment on May 1.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_2004,_pp.10-11_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_2004,_pp.10-11-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> During his early naval career Decatur learned the arts of naval war under Barry, and also James Barron, both of whom took a liking to Decatur.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To ensure his son's success in his naval career, the senior Decatur hired a tutor, Talbot Hamilton, a former officer of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, to instruct his son in navigational and nautical sciences. While serving aboard <i>United States</i> Decatur received what was the equivalent to formal naval training not only from Hamilton but through active service aboard a commissioned ship, which is something that distinguished the young midshipman from many of his contemporaries.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>  He also had a talent for drawing ships and designing and building ship models and when time allowed would also pursue this hobby.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis,_1937_p.7_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis,_1937_p.7-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Quasi-War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Quasi-War" title="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:266px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Constellation.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/USS_Constellation.jpg/264px-USS_Constellation.jpg" decoding="async" width="264" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/USS_Constellation.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="348" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USS_Constellation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>USS <i>Constellation</i>,<br />the first U.S. Navy vessel put to sea</center></div></div></div>
<p>Once the United States won its independence and no longer had the protection of Britain, it was faced with the task of protecting its own ships and interests. There were few American ships capable of defending the American coastline, much less of protecting <a href="/wiki/Merchant_vessel" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant vessel">merchant ships</a> at sea and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  The few warships that were available were converted into merchant ships. The French in particular were outraged that America was still involved in trading with Britain, a country with whom they were at war, and because of American refusal to pay a debt that was owed to the French crown, which had just been overthrown by the newly established French Republic. As a result, France began intercepting American ships that were involved in trading with Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guttridge1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guttridge1-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> This provocation prompted President <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">Adams</a> to appoint <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Stoddert" title="Benjamin Stoddert">Benjamin Stoddert</a> as the first Secretary of the Navy. Stoddert immediately ordered his senior commanders to "subdue, seize and take any armed vessel or vessels sailing under the authority or pretense of authority, from the French Republic."<sup id="cite_ref-Guttridge1_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guttridge1-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> At this time, moreover, America was not even ranked with European naval forces.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 22, 1799, Decatur was promoted to lieutenant by President <a href="/wiki/John_Adams" title="John Adams">John Adams</a><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> after serving for more than a year as midshipman aboard the frigate <i>United States</i>.  While <i>United States</i> was undergoing repairs Decatur received orders to remain in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> to recruit and assemble a crew for the vessel. While there, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_mate" title="Chief mate">chief mate</a> of an <a href="/wiki/East_Indiaman" title="East Indiaman">Indiaman</a>, using foul language, made several derogatory remarks about Decatur and the U.S. Navy, apparently because he had lost some of his crew to Decatur's recruiting efforts. Decatur remained calm and left the scene without further incident. When he related the matter to his father, however, Captain Decatur stressed that the honor of the family and of the Navy had been insulted and that his son should return and challenge the chief mate to a duel. Stephen's friend and shipmate, Lieutenant Somers, was sent ahead with a letter from Decatur asking if an apology could be obtained from the man. Refusing to apologize, the chief mate instead accepted Decatur's challenge and secured a location for the duel. Decatur, being an expert shot with a pistol, told his friend Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_(1778%E2%80%931869)" title="Charles Stewart (1778–1869)">Charles Stewart</a> that he believed his opponent not to be as able and he would thus endeavour to only wound his opponent in the hip, which is exactly how the duel turned out. The honor and courage of both duelists having been satisfied, the matter was resolved without a fatality.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By July 1, 1799, <i>United States</i> had been refitted and repaired and commenced its mission to patrol the south Atlantic coast and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> in search of French ships which were preying on American merchant vessels. After completing this mission the ship was taken to <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk, Virginia</a>, for minor repairs and then set sail for <a href="/wiki/Newport,_Rhode_Island" title="Newport, Rhode Island">Newport, Rhode Island</a>, arriving on September 12. While the ship was berthed there, Commodore Barry received orders to prepare for a voyage to transport two U.S. envoys to Spain and on December 3 sailed on <i>United States</i> for <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> via England. During the crossing the ship encountered <a href="/wiki/Gale_force" class="mw-redirect" title="Gale force">gale force</a> winds, and at their insistence the two envoys were dropped off at the nearest port in England.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Upon returning home and arriving on the <a href="/wiki/Delaware_River" title="Delaware River">Delaware River</a> on April 3, 1800, it was discovered that <i>United States</i> had incurred damage from the storms she had weathered at sea. Consequently, the vessel was taken up the Delaware to <a href="/wiki/Chester,_Pennsylvania" title="Chester, Pennsylvania">Chester, Pennsylvania</a>, for repairs.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Not wanting to remain with <i>United States</i> during the months of repairs and outfitting, Decatur obtained a transfer to the brig <a href="/wiki/USS_Norfolk_(1798)" title="USS Norfolk (1798)">USS&#160;<i>Norfolk</i></a><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> under the command of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Calvert" title="Thomas Calvert">Thomas Calvert</a>. In May the <i>Norfolk</i> sailed to the West Indies to patrol its waters looking for French privateers and <a href="/wiki/Men-of-war" class="mw-redirect" title="Men-of-war">men-of-war</a>. During the months that followed 25 armed enemy craft were captured or destroyed. With orders to rendezvous with merchantmen bound for America, <i>Norfolk</i> continued on to <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Colombia" title="Cartagena, Colombia">Cartagena (Colombia)</a> with orders to escort the ships back to the United States, protecting them from pirates and privateers.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur transferred back to <i>United States</i> by June 1800; with extra guns and sails and improved structure the refurbished ship made her way down the Delaware River. Aboard ship at this time were Decatur's former classmates Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_(1778%E2%80%931869)" title="Charles Stewart (1778–1869)">Charles Stewart</a> and Midshipman <a href="/wiki/Richard_Somers" title="Richard Somers">Richard Somers</a>, along with Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/James_Barron" title="James Barron">James Barron</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the Quasi-War, the U.S. Navy underwent a significant reduction of active ships and officers; Decatur was one of the few selected to remain commissioned. By the time hostilities with France came to a close, America had a renewed appreciation for the value of a navy. By 1801 the American Navy consisted of 42 naval vessels, three of which were <a href="/wiki/USS_President_(1800)" title="USS President (1800)">USS&#160;<i>President</i></a>, <i>Constellation</i> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Chesapeake_(1799)" title="USS Chesapeake (1799)">USS&#160;<i>Chesapeake</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Barbary_War">First Barbary War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First Barbary War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:342px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_coast3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Barbary_coast3.jpg/340px-Barbary_coast3.jpg" decoding="async" width="340" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Barbary_coast3.jpg/510px-Barbary_coast3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Barbary_coast3.jpg/680px-Barbary_coast3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="974" data-file-height="582" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_coast3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Barbary Coast of North Africa</div></div></div>
<p>The first war against the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Coast" title="Barbary Coast">Barbary States</a> was in response to the frequent piracy of American vessels in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> and the capture and <a href="/wiki/Barbary_slave_trade" title="Barbary slave trade">enslavement</a> of American crews for huge ransoms. President <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Jefferson</a>, known for his aversion to standing armies and the navy, acted contrary to such sentiment and began his presidency by sending U.S. naval forces to fight the Barbary states rather than continue paying huge annual tributes to the <a href="/wiki/Petty_kingdom" title="Petty kingdom">petty</a> North African kingdoms.  On May 13, 1801, at the beginning of the war, Decatur was assigned duty aboard the frigate <a href="/wiki/USS_Essex_(1799)" title="USS Essex (1799)">USS&#160;<i>Essex</i></a> to serve as the first lieutenant. <i>Essex</i>, bearing 32 guns, was commanded by <a href="/wiki/William_Bainbridge" title="William Bainbridge">William Bainbridge</a> and was attached to Commodore <a href="/wiki/Richard_Dale" title="Richard Dale">Richard Dale</a>'s squadron<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> which also included <a href="/wiki/USS_Philadelphia_(1799)" title="USS Philadelphia (1799)">USS&#160;<i>Philadelphia</i></a>, <i>President</i> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Enterprise_(1799)" title="USS Enterprise (1799)">USS&#160;<i>Enterprise</i></a>. Departing for the Mediterranean on June 1, this squadron was the first American naval squadron to cross the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 1, after encountering and being forestalled by adverse winds, the squadron sailed into the Mediterranean with the mission to confront the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a>. Arriving at <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>, Commodore Dale learned that <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> had already declared war upon the United States.  At this time there were two Tripolitan warships of sizable consequence berthed in Gibraltar's harbour, but their captains claimed that they had no knowledge of the war. Dale assumed they were about to embark on the Atlantic to prey on American merchant ships. With orders to sail for <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> and Tripoli, Dale ordered that <i>Philadelphia</i> be left behind to guard the Tripolitan vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 1802, Decatur transferred to the 36-gun frigate <a href="/wiki/USS_New_York_(1800)" title="USS New York (1800)">USS&#160;<i>New York</i></a> as 1st Lieutenant under Commodore <a href="/wiki/James_Barron" title="James Barron">James Barron</a>. While en route to Tripoli the five-ship squadron to which <i>New York</i> was attached encountered gale-force winds, lasting more than a week, which forced the squadron to put up in <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>. While there Decatur and another American officer were involved in a personal confrontation with a British officer which resulted in Decatur returning to the United States. There he took temporary command of the newly built 18-gun <a href="/wiki/Brig" title="Brig">brig</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Argus_(1803)" title="USS Argus (1803)">USS&#160;<i>Argus</i></a><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> which he sailed to Gibraltar, relinquishing command of the ship upon arrival to Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Hull" title="Isaac Hull">Isaac Hull</a>. In exchange Decatur was given command of <i>Enterprise</i>, a 12-gun <a href="/wiki/Schooner" title="Schooner">schooner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 23, 1803, <i>Enterprise</i> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Constitution" title="USS Constitution">USS&#160;<i>Constitution</i></a> confronted the Tripolitan <a href="/wiki/Ketch" title="Ketch">ketch</a> <i>Mastico</i> sailing under <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Turkey.svg" title="File:Flag of Turkey.svg">Turkish colors</a>, armed with only two guns and sailing without passports on her way to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> from Tripoli. On board were a small number of Tripolitan soldiers. After a brief engagement Decatur and his crew captured the ship, killing or wounding the few men defending the vessel. After its capture the small ship was taken to <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily" title="Syracuse, Sicily">Syracuse</a>, condemned by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Preble" title="Edward Preble">Commodore Preble</a> as a legitimate <a href="/wiki/Prize_of_war" title="Prize of war">prize of war</a>, and given a new name, <a href="/wiki/USS_Intrepid_(1798)" title="USS Intrepid (1798)">USS&#160;<i>Intrepid</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burning_of_USS_Philadelphia">Burning of USS <i>Philadelphia</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Burning of USS Philadelphia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Capture_Philadelphia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Capture_Philadelphia.jpg/320px-Capture_Philadelphia.jpg" decoding="async" width="320" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Capture_Philadelphia.jpg/480px-Capture_Philadelphia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Capture_Philadelphia.jpg/640px-Capture_Philadelphia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1989" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Capture_Philadelphia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>Grounding and capture of USS <i>Philadelphia</i></center></div></div></div>
<p>On October 31, 1803, <i>Philadelphia</i>, under the command of Commodore <a href="/wiki/William_Bainbridge" title="William Bainbridge">William Bainbridge</a>, ran aground on an uncharted reef (known as Kaliusa reef) near Tripoli's harbor. After desperate and failed attempts to refloat the ship she was subsequently captured and her crew imprisoned by Tripolitan forces. After coming up with an elaborate plan,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Decatur sailed for Tripoli with 80 volunteers (most of them being U.S. Marines) intending to enter the harbor with <i>Intrepid</i> without suspicion to board and set ablaze the frigate <i>Philadelphia</i>, denying its use to the corsairs. <a href="/wiki/USS_Syren_(1803)" title="USS Syren (1803)">USS&#160;<i>Syren</i></a>,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> commanded by Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Charles_Stewart_(1778%E2%80%931869)" title="Charles Stewart (1778–1869)">Charles Stewart</a>, accompanied <i>Intrepid</i> to provide supporting fire during and after the assault. Before entering the harbor eight sailors from <i>Syren</i> boarded <i>Intrepid</i>, including <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Macdonough" title="Thomas Macdonough">Thomas Macdonough</a> who had recently served aboard <i>Philadelphia</i> and knew the ship's layout intimately.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Decatur established a close friendship with Macdonough and became his mentor during the course of their careers.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On February 16, 1804, at seven o'clock in the evening under the dim light of a waxing crescent moon, <i>Intrepid</i> slowly sailed into Tripoli harbor. Decatur's vessel was made to look like a common merchant ship from Malta and was outfitted with <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" title="File:Flag of the United Kingdom.svg">British colours</a>. To further avoid suspicion, on board were five Sicilian volunteers including the pilot Salvatore Catalano, who spoke <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>. The boarding party remained hidden below in position, prepared to board the captured <i>Philadelphia</i>. The men were divided into several groups, each assigned to secure given areas of the ship, with the additional explicit instruction of refraining from the use of firearms unless it proved absolutely necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> As Decatur's ship came closer to <i>Philadelphia</i>, Catalano called out to the harbor personnel in Arabic that their ship had lost its anchors during a recent storm and was seeking refuge at Tripoli for repairs.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> By 9:30&#160;p.m. Decatur's ship was within 200 yards of <i>Philadelphia</i>, whose <a href="/wiki/Yard_(sailing)" title="Yard (sailing)">lower yards</a> were now resting on the deck with her foremast missing, as Bainbridge had ordered it cut away and had also jettisoned some of her guns in a futile effort to refloat the ship by lightening her load.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg/240px-Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="355" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg/360px-Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg/480px-Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3407" data-file-height="5033" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burning_of_the_uss_philadelphia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>Burning of the <a href="/wiki/USS_Philadelphia_(1799)" title="USS Philadelphia (1799)">USS&#160;<i>Philadelphia</i></a><br />by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Moran" title="Edward Moran">Edward Moran</a> (1897)<br /><i>Intrepid</i> depicted in foreground</center></div></div></div>
<p>As Decatur approached the berthed <i>Philadelphia</i> he encountered a light wind that made his approach tedious. He had to casually position his ship close enough to <i>Philadelphia</i> to allow his men to board while not creating any suspicion. When the two vessels were finally close enough, Catalano obtained permission for Decatur to tie <i>Intrepid</i> to the captured <i>Philadelphia</i>. Decatur surprised the few Tripolitans on board when he shouted the order "board!", signaling to the hidden crew below to emerge and storm the captured ship.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Without losing a single man, Decatur and 60 of his men, dressed as Maltese sailors or Arab seamen and armed with swords and boarding <a href="/wiki/Pike_(weapon)" title="Pike (weapon)">pikes</a>, boarded and reclaimed <i>Philadelphia</i> in less than 10 minutes, killing at least 20 of the Tripolitan crew, capturing one wounded crewman, and forcing the rest to flee by jumping overboard. Only one of Decatur's men was slightly wounded by a <a href="/wiki/Saber" class="mw-redirect" title="Saber">saber</a> blade. There was hope that the small boarding crew could launch the captured ship, but the vessel was in no condition to set sail for the open sea. Decatur soon realized that the small <i>Intrepid</i> could not tow the larger and heavier warship out of the harbor. Commodore Preble's order to Decatur was to destroy the ship where she berthed as a last resort, if <i>Philadelphia</i> was unseaworthy. With the ship secure, Decatur's crew began placing combustibles about <i>Philadelphia</i> with orders to set her ablaze. After making sure the fire was large enough to sustain itself, Decatur ordered his men to abandon the ship and was the last man to leave <i>Philadelphia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>  As the flames intensified, the guns aboard <i>Philadelphia</i>, all loaded and ready for battle, became heated and began discharging, some firing into the town and shore batteries, while the ropes securing the ship burned off, allowing the vessel to drift into the rocks at the western entrance of the harbor.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While <i>Intrepid</i> was under fire from the Tripolitans who were now gathering along the shore and in small boats, the larger <i>Syren</i> was nearby providing covering fire at the Tripolitan shore batteries and gunboats. Decatur and his men left the burning vessel in Tripoli's harbor and set sail for the open sea, barely escaping in the confusion. With the cover of night helping to obscure the enemy gunfire, <i>Intrepid</i> and <i>Syren</i> made their way back to Syracuse, arriving February 18.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> After learning of Decatur's daring capture and destruction of <i>Philadelphia</i> without suffering a single fatality, British Vice Admiral Lord <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Nelson" class="mw-redirect" title="Horatio Nelson">Horatio Nelson</a>, who at the time was blockading the French port at <a href="/wiki/Toulon" title="Toulon">Toulon</a>, is said to have stated it was "the most bold and daring act of the Age."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Decatur's daring and successful burning of <i>Philadelphia</i> made him an immediate national hero in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis,_1937_p.43_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis,_1937_p.43-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Appreciation for the efforts of Preble and Decatur were not limited to their peers and countrymen. At <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Naples</a>, Decatur was praised and dubbed "Terror of the Foe" by the local media. Upon hearing the news of their victory in Tripoli, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_VII" title="Pope Pius VII">Pope Pius VII</a> publicly declared that "the United States, though in their infancy, had done more to humble and humiliate the anti-Christian barbarians on the African coast in one night than all the European states had done for a long period of time."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Upon his return to Syracuse, Decatur resumed command of <i>Enterprise</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_attack_on_Tripoli">Second attack on Tripoli</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Second attack on Tripoli">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Barbary_War" title="First Barbary War">First Barbary War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg/250px-Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg/375px-Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg/500px-Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5079" data-file-height="3717" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Decatur_Boarding_the_Tripolitan_Gunboat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Decatur Boarding the Tripolitan Gunboat</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Malone_Carter" title="Dennis Malone Carter">Dennis Malone Carter</a></div></div></div>
<p>With the significant victory achieved with the burning of  <i>Philadelphia</i>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Preble" title="Edward Preble">Preble</a> now had reason to believe that bringing Tripoli to peaceful terms was in sight. Preble planned another attack on Tripoli and amassed a squadron consisting of the frigate <i>Constitution</i>, the brigs <i>Syren</i>, <i>Argus</i> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Scourge_(1804)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Scourge (1804)"><i>Scourge</i></a>, and the schooners <a href="/wiki/USS_Nautilus_(1799)" title="USS Nautilus (1799)"><i>Nautilus</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Vixen_(1803)" title="USS Vixen (1803)"><i>Vixen</i></a> and <i>Enterprise</i>, towing gunboats and ketches.
</p><p>For the coming attack Preble borrowed six gunboats from <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Ferdinand I of the Two Sicilies">King Ferdinand I</a> of the Two Sicilies who was also at war with Tripoli. Light vessels with shallow drafts were needed to make their way about in the shallow and confined waters of Tripoli's harbor.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> Making their way into the west end of Tripoli harbor, they began bombarding Tripoli on August 3, 1804.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Symonds30_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Symonds30-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Preble divided his gunboats into two divisions, putting Decatur in command of the second division. At 1:30 Preble raised his signal flag to begin the attack on Tripoli. It was elaborate and well planned, brigs, schooners and bomb ketches coming into the attack at various stages.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The Tripolitan <a href="/wiki/Pasha" title="Pasha">pasha</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Murad_Reis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Murad Reis (page does not exist)">Murad Reis</a>, was expecting the attack and had his own gunboats lined up and waiting at various locations within the harbor.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout the month of August 1804 Preble used these gunboats to launch a series of furious attacks on Tripoli, forcing the residents to flee into the country-side. During this time Decatur in command of the gunboats captured three Tripolitan gunboats and sank three others.<sup id="cite_ref-Symonds30_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Symonds30-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The Tripolitans also inflicted considerable damage on some of the attacking vessels; Decatur's ship was struck with a 24-pound shot through her hull above the waterline. Before the battle ended <a href="/wiki/USS_John_Adams_(1799)" title="USS John Adams (1799)">USS&#160;<i>John Adams</i></a>, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Chauncey" title="Isaac Chauncey">Isaac Chauncey</a>, arrived on the scene. On board the vessel were official documents promoting Decatur to the rank of <a href="/wiki/Captain_(naval)" title="Captain (naval)">captain</a>. <i>John Adams</i> also brought news that, upon the loss of the frigate <i>Philadelphia</i>, the government was sending four additional frigates, <i>President</i>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Congress_(1799)" title="USS Congress (1799)"><i>Congress</i></a>, <i>Constellation</i> and <i>Essex</i>, to Tripoli with enough force to convince the Pasha of Tripoli that peace was his only viable alternative. Because Preble's rank was not high enough for this command <i>John Adams</i> also brought the news that he would have to surrender command to Commodore Barron.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The fighting between the squadrons and the bombarding of Tripoli lasted three hours, with Preble's squadrons emerging victorious.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  However, success and promotion were overshadowed by an unfortunate turn of events for Decatur. During the fighting Decatur's younger brother, <a href="/w/index.php?title=James_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James Decatur (page does not exist)">James Decatur</a>, in command of a gunboat, was mortally wounded by a Tripolitan captain during the boarding of a vessel feigning surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Midshipman Brown, who was next in command after James, managed to break away from the ambushing vessel and immediately approached Decatur's gunboat bringing the news of his brother's fatal injury. Decatur had just captured his first Tripolitan vessel and upon receiving the news turned command of his captured prize over to Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Thorn" title="Jonathan Thorn">Jonathan Thorn</a> and immediately set out to avenge his brother's treacherous injury.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> After catching up with and pulling alongside the Tripolitan ship, Decatur was the first to board the enemy vessel with Midshipman Macdonough at his heels along with nine volunteer crew members.  Decatur and his crew were outnumbered 5 to 1 but were organized and kept their form, fighting furiously side by side.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>  Decatur had little trouble singling out the corsair captain, the man responsible for James' mortal wound, and immediately engaged the man. He was a large and formidable man in Muslim garb, and armed with a boarding pike he thrust his weapon at Decatur's chest. Armed with a <a href="/wiki/Cutlass" title="Cutlass">cutlass</a> Decatur deflected the lunge, breaking his own weapon at the hilt.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>  During the fight Decatur was almost killed by another Tripolitan crew member, but his life was spared by the already wounded <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Frazier" title="Daniel Frazier">Daniel Frazier</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> a crewman who threw himself over Decatur just in time, receiving a blow intended for Decatur to his own head. The struggle continued, with the Tripolitan captain, being larger and stronger than Decatur, gaining the upper hand. Armed with a dagger the Tripolitan attempted to stab Decatur in the heart, but while wrestling the arm of his adversary, Decatur managed to take hold of his pistol and fired a shot <a href="/wiki/Point-blank_range" title="Point-blank range">point-blank</a>, immediately killing his formidable foe.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> When the fighting was over, 21 Tripolitans were dead with only three taken alive.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later James Decatur was taken aboard <i>Constitution</i> where he was joined by his brother Stephen, who stayed with him until he had died. The next day, after a funeral and military ceremony that was conducted by Preble, Stephen Decatur saw his brother's remains committed to the depths of the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When a good number of days passed without the reinforcements of ships promised by president <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Jefferson</a>, the attack on Tripoli was renewed by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Preble" title="Edward Preble">Preble</a> on August 24. As the days passed, Tripoli showed no signs of surrender, which now prompted Preble to devise another plan. <i>Intrepid</i>, the same ship that captured <i>Philadelphia</i>, was loaded with barrels of gunpowder and other ordnance and sent sailing into a group of Tripolitan vessels defending the harbor. The attack on the harbor and Tripoli proved successful and ultimately caused the Bashaw of Tripoli to consider surrender and the return of American prisoners held captive, including Commodore Bainbridge of <i>Philadelphia</i>, who had been held prisoner since October 1803 when that ship was captured after running aground near Tripoli harbor. On June 4, 1805, the Bashaw of Tripoli finally surrendered and signed a peace treaty with the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Command_of_USS_Constitution">Command of USS <i>Constitution</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Command of USS Constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:248px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Constitution1803.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Constitution1803.jpg/246px-Constitution1803.jpg" decoding="async" width="246" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Constitution1803.jpg/369px-Constitution1803.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Constitution1803.jpg/492px-Constitution1803.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="5578" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Constitution1803.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>USS <i>Constitution</i></center></div></div></div>
<p>Shortly after his recapture and destruction of <i>Philadelphia</i>, Decatur was given command of the frigate <i>Constitution</i>, a post he held from October 28 to November 9, 1804.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Upon the day of Decatur's return with <i>Intrepid</i>, <a href="/wiki/Edward_Preble" title="Edward Preble">Commodore Preble</a> wrote to Secretary of the Navy <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Stoddert" title="Benjamin Stoddert">Benjamin Stoddert</a> recommending to President Jefferson that Decatur be promoted to captain. Decatur was promoted to captain with the date of rank February 16, 1804.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> He was promoted to captain at the age twenty-five, largely for his daring capture and destruction of <i>Philadelphia</i> <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Tripoli_Harbor" title="Second Battle of Tripoli Harbor">in Tripoli's harbor</a>, making him the youngest man ever to hold the rank.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 10, 1804, <a href="/wiki/James_Barron" title="James Barron">Commodore Barron</a> arrived at Tripoli with two ships, <i>President</i> and <i>Constellation</i>, whereupon Commodore Preble relinquished command of his blockading squadron to him.  Before returning to the United States he sailed to Malta in <i>Constitution</i> on September 14, so it could be caulked and refitted. From there he sailed to Syracuse in <i>Argus</i>, where on September 24 he ordered Decatur to sail this vessel back to Malta to take command of <i>Constitution</i>. From here Decatur sailed <i>Constitution</i> back to Tripoli to join <i>Constellation</i> and <i>Congress</i>, the blockading force stationed there now under the command of Commodore Barron. On November 6, he relinquished command of <i>Constitution</i> to Commodore <a href="/wiki/John_Rodgers_(1772%E2%80%931838)" title="John Rodgers (1772–1838)">John Rodgers</a>, his senior, in exchange for the smaller vessel <i>Congress</i>. In need of new sails and other repairs Rodgers sailed <i>Constitution</i> to Lisbon on November 27, where it remained for approximately six weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On March 8, 1806, Decatur married Susan Wheeler, the daughter of Luke Wheeler, the mayor of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">Norfolk, Virginia</a>. She was well known for her beauty and intelligence among Norfolk and Washington society. They had met at a dinner and ball held by the mayor for a <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisian</a> ambassador who was in the United States negotiating peace terms for his country's recent defeat at <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> under the silent guns of <a href="/wiki/John_Rodgers_(1772%E2%80%931838)" title="John Rodgers (1772–1838)">John Rodgers</a> and Decatur.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Before marrying Susan, Decatur had already vowed to serve in the U.S. Navy and maintained that to abandon his service to his country for personal reasons would make him unworthy of her hand. Susan was once pursued by Vice President <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Bonaparte" title="Jérôme Bonaparte">Jérôme Bonaparte</a>, brother to <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>, both of whom she turned down. For several months after their marriage the couple resided with Susan's parents in Norfolk, after which Stephen received orders sending him to Newport to supervise the building of gunboats.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lewis,_1937_p.89_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis,_1937_p.89-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The couple never had children during their fourteen years of marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_1937_p.174_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_1937_p.174-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supervision_of_shipbuilding">Supervision of shipbuilding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Supervision of shipbuilding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the spring of 1806, Decatur was given command of a squadron of <a href="/wiki/Gunboat" title="Gunboat">gunboats</a> stationed in the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a> at Norfolk, Virginia, the home of his future wife, Susan Wheeler. He had long requested such an assignment; however, one of his colleagues believed that his request was also motivated by a desire to be close to Wheeler. While stationed here Decatur took the opportunity to court Miss Wheeler, whom he would soon marry that year. After their marriage in March, Decatur lived with his wife's family in Norfolk until June when Secretary of the Navy <a href="/wiki/Robert_Smith_(Cabinet_member)" title="Robert Smith (Cabinet member)">Robert Smith</a> gave him orders to supervise the building of four gunboats at Newport, Rhode Island, and four others in Connecticut of which he would later take command.  Having drawn many illustrations of and designed and built many models of ships, along with having experience as a ship builder and designer from when he was employed at Gurney and Smith in 1797 while overseeing the construction of the frigate <i>United States</i>, Decatur was a natural choice for this new position. Decatur and his wife Susan lived together all through this period.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis,_1937_p.89_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis,_1937_p.89-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_1937_p.11_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_1937_p.11-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Chesapeake.E2.80.93Leopard_Affair"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Chesapeake–Leopard_Affair"><i>Chesapeake</i>–<i>Leopard</i> Affair</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Chesapeake–Leopard Affair">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake%E2%80%93Leopard_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesapeake–Leopard Affair">Chesapeake–Leopard Affair</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leopardchesapeake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Leopardchesapeake.jpg/280px-Leopardchesapeake.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Leopardchesapeake.jpg/420px-Leopardchesapeake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Leopardchesapeake.jpg/560px-Leopardchesapeake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="738" data-file-height="378" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leopardchesapeake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>HMS <i>Leopard</i> engaging USS <i>Chesapeake</i></div></div></div>
<p>After overseeing the completion of gunboats, Decatur returned to Norfolk in March 1807 and was given command of the <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Naval_Shipyard" title="Norfolk Naval Shipyard">Naval Yard at Gosport</a>.  While commissioned there he received a letter from the residing British consul to turn over three deserters from the British ship <i>Melampus</i> who had enlisted in the American Navy through <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Sinclair" title="Arthur Sinclair">Lieutenant Arthur Sinclair</a>, who was recruiting crew members for <i>Chesapeake</i>, which was at this time in Washington being outfitted for its coming voyage to the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Since the recruiting party was not under the command of Decatur, he refused to intervene. Sinclair also declined to take any action, claiming that he did not have the authority or any such orders from a superior officer. The matter was then referred to the British minister at Washington, a Mr. Erskine, who in turn referred the matter to the Navy Department through Commodore Barron, demanding that the three deserters be surrendered to British authority. It was soon discovered that the deserters were Americans who were forcibly impressed into the British Navy, and since the existing American treaty with Britain only pertained to criminal fugitives of justice, not deserters in the military, Barron accordingly also refused to turn them over.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Soon thereafter <i>Chesapeake</i> left Norfolk, and after stopping briefly at Washington for further preparations, set sail for the Mediterranean on June 22. In little time she was pursued by <a href="/wiki/HMS_Leopard_(1790)" title="HMS Leopard (1790)">HMS&#160;<i>Leopard</i></a>, which at the time was part of a British squadron in <a href="/wiki/Lynnhaven_River" title="Lynnhaven River">Lynnhaven Bay</a>. Upon closing with <i>Chesapeake</i>, Barron was hailed by the captain of <i>Leopard</i> and informed and a demand from Vice-Admiral Humphreys that <i>Chesapeake</i> be searched for deserters. Barron found the demand extraordinary and when he refused to surrender any of his crew, <i>Leopard</i> soon opened fire on <i>Chesapeake</i>. Having just put to sea, <i>Chesapeake</i> was not prepared to do battle and was unable to return fire. Inside twenty minutes, three of her crew were killed and eighteen wounded. Barron struck the ship's colors<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> and surrendered his ship, whereupon she was boarded and the alleged deserters were taken into British custody. News of the incident soon reached President Jefferson, the Department of the Navy and Decatur, who  was outraged, was the one who was first confronted with the matter. The incident soon came to be referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake%E2%80%93Leopard_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesapeake–Leopard Affair"><i>Chesapeake</i>–<i>Leopard</i> Affair</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> an event whose controversy would lead to a duel between Barron and Decatur some years later, as Decatur served on Barron's <a href="/wiki/Court-martial" title="Court-martial">court-martial</a> and later was one of the most outspoken critics of the questionable handling of <i>Chesapeake</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Toll,_2006_p.470_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toll,_2006_p.470-118">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Command_of_USS_Chesapeake">Command of USS <i>Chesapeake</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Command of USS Chesapeake">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:266px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USSChesapeake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/USSChesapeake.jpg/264px-USSChesapeake.jpg" decoding="async" width="264" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/USSChesapeake.jpg/396px-USSChesapeake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/USSChesapeake.jpg/528px-USSChesapeake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="486" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USSChesapeake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>USS <i>Chesapeake</i></center></div></div></div>
<p>On June 26, 1807, Decatur was appointed to command <i>Chesapeake</i>, a 44-gun frigate, along with command of all gunboats at Norfolk.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>  <i>Chesapeake</i> had just returned to Norfolk after repairs to damage incurred during the <i>Chesapeake</i>–<i>Leopard</i> Affair. Commodore Barron had just been relieved of command following his court martial over the incident. Decatur was a member of that court martial, which had found Barron guilty of "unpreparedness", barring him from command for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, Barron's previous orders to sail for the Mediterranean were canceled and <i>Chesapeake</i> was instead assigned to Commodore Decatur, with a squadron of gunboats, to patrol the <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> coast enforcing the <a href="/wiki/Embargo_Act_of_1807" title="Embargo Act of 1807">Embargo Act</a> throughout 1809. Unable to command, Barron left the country for <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> and remained there through the War of 1812.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>  Before Decatur assumed command of <i>Chesapeake</i> he learned from observers, and then informed the Navy Secretary, that the British ships <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bellona_(1806)" title="HMS Bellona (1806)">HMS&#160;<i>Bellona</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Triumph_(1764)" title="HMS Triumph (1764)">HMS&#160;<i>Triumph</i></a> were lightening their ballasts to prepare for a blockade at Norfolk.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
During this segment of his life, Decatur's father, Stephen Decatur Sr., died in November 1808 at the relatively young age of 57, with his mother's death following the next year. Both parents were buried at <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church,_Philadelphia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter&#39;s Church, Philadelphia">St. Peter's Church</a> in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Command_of_USS_United_States">Command of USS <i>United States</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Command of USS United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USSUnitedStates1797.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/USSUnitedStates1797.jpg/220px-USSUnitedStates1797.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/USSUnitedStates1797.jpg/330px-USSUnitedStates1797.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/USSUnitedStates1797.jpg/440px-USSUnitedStates1797.jpg 2x" data-file-width="682" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USSUnitedStates1797.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>USS <i>United States</i></center></div></div></div>
<p>In May 1810 Decatur was appointed commander of <i>United States</i>, a heavy frigate with 44 guns. This was the same vessel that he supervised the building of while employed at Gurney and Smith, and the same ship, then under the command of <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">John Barry</a>, on which he had commenced his naval career as midshipman in 1798. The frigate had just been commissioned and was outfitted and supplied for service at sea. After taking command of <i>United States</i>, now the rallying point of the young American Navy, Decatur sailed to most of the naval ports on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">eastern seaboard</a> and was well received at each stop.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On May 21, 1811, he sailed <i>United States</i> from Norfolk along with <a href="/wiki/USS_Hornet_(1805_brig)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Hornet (1805 brig)">USS&#160;<i>Hornet</i></a> on assignment to patrol the coast, returning to Norfolk on November 23 of that year. In 1812 he sailed with <i>Argus</i> and <i>Congress</i> but were soon recalled upon receiving news about the outbreak of war with Britain. There Decatur joined Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Rodgers_(1772%E2%80%931838)" title="John Rodgers (1772–1838)">John Rodgers</a>, commander of <i>President</i> and his squadron. On this cruise Rodgers failed to accomplish his mission of intercepting the fleet of English West-Indiamen. On August 31, Decatur sailed <i>United States</i> to Boston. On October 8, he sailed a second cruise with Rodgers' squadron.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="War_of_1812">War of 1812</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: War of 1812">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen-Decatur3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Stephen-Decatur3.jpg/220px-Stephen-Decatur3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="297" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Stephen-Decatur3.jpg/330px-Stephen-Decatur3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Stephen-Decatur3.jpg/440px-Stephen-Decatur3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="624" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stephen-Decatur3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stephen Decatur by <a href="/wiki/Alonzo_Chappel" title="Alonzo Chappel">Alonzo Chappel</a></div></div></div>
<p>The desire for expansion into the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>, the capture and impressment of American citizens into the Royal Navy along with British alliance with, and recruitment of, American Indian tribes against America, were all events that led into the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Intended to avoid war, the <a href="/wiki/Embargo_Act_of_1807" title="Embargo Act of 1807">Embargo Act</a> only compounded matters that led to war.  Finally on June 18, 1812, the United States declared war on Great Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>  By 1814 Britain had committed nearly 100 warships along the American coast and other points. Consequently, the war was fought mostly in the naval theater where Decatur and other naval officers played major roles in the success of the United States' efforts during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Upon the onset of the war President <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> ordered several naval vessels to be dispatched to patrol the American coastline. The U.S. flagships <i>President</i>, <i>Essex</i> and the <i>Hornet</i>  were joined in lower <a href="/wiki/New_York_harbor" class="mw-redirect" title="New York harbor">New York harbor</a> by <i>United States</i> commanded by Decatur,  <i>Congress</i>, and <i>Argus</i>. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> had originally considered a plan that would simply use U.S. naval vessels as barriers guarding their entrances, but the unpopular plan never materialized.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Three days after the United States declared war against Britain, a squadron under the command of Commodore <a href="/wiki/John_Rodgers_(1772%E2%80%931838)" title="John Rodgers (1772–1838)">John Rodgers</a> in <i>President</i>, along with Commodore Stephen Decatur of <i>United States</i>, <i>Argus</i>, <i>Essex</i> and <i>Hornet</i>, departed from the harbor at New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> As soon as Rodgers received news of the declaration of war, fearing that the order to confine naval ships to port would be reconsidered by Congress, he and his squadron departed New York bay within the hour. The squadron patrolled the waters off the American upper east coast until the end of August, their first objective being a British fleet reported to have recently departed from the West Indies.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_captures_Macedonian"><i>United States</i> captures <i>Macedonian</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: United States captures Macedonian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/USS_United_States_vs_HMS_Macedonian" title="USS United States vs HMS Macedonian">USS United States vs HMS Macedonian</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg/280px-BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="234" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg/420px-BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg/560px-BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BirchBattleBetweenTheUnitedStatesAndTheMacedonian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Engagement_between_the_United_States_and_the_Macedonian" title="Engagement between the United States and the Macedonian"><i>United States</i> engaging <i>Macedonian</i></a>, by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Birch_(artist)" title="Thomas Birch (artist)">Thomas Birch</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rodgers' squadron again sailed on October 8, 1812, this time from Boston, Massachusetts. Three days later, after capturing <i>Mandarin</i>, Decatur separated from Rodgers and his squadron and with <i>United States</i> continued to cruise eastward. At dawn on October 25, five hundred miles south of the <a href="/wiki/File:Locator_map_of_Azores_in_EU.svg" title="File:Locator map of Azores in EU.svg">Azores</a>, lookouts on board reported seeing a sail 12 miles to windward. As the ship slowly rose over the horizon, Captain Decatur made out the fine, familiar lines of <a href="/wiki/HMS_Macedonian" title="HMS Macedonian">HMS&#160;<i>Macedonian</i></a>, a British frigate bearing 38 guns.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Macedonian</i> and <i>United States</i> had been berthed next to one another in 1810, in port at Norfolk, Virginia.
