The British captain <a href="/wiki/John_Surman_Carden" title="John Surman Carden">John Carden</a> bet a fur <a href="/wiki/Beaver_hat" title="Beaver hat">beaver hat</a> that if the two ever met in battle, <i>Macedonian</i> would emerge victorious.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> However, the engagement in a heavy swell proved otherwise as <i>United States</i> pounded <i><sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_1937_p.11_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_1937_p.11-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></i> <i>Macedonian</i> into a dismasted wreck from long range.  During the engagement Decatur was standing on a box of shot when he was knocked down almost unconscious when a flying splinter struck him in the chest. Wounded, he soon recovered and was on his feet in command again.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Because of the greater range of the guns aboard <i>United States</i>, Decatur and his crew got off seventy broadsides, with <i>Macedonian</i> only getting off thirty, and consequently emerged from the battle relatively unscathed.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <i>Macedonian</i> had no option but surrender, and thus was taken as a prize by Decatur. Eager to present the nation with a prize, Decatur and his crew spent two weeks repairing and refitting the captured British frigate to prepare it for its journey across the Atlantic to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blockade_at_New_London">Blockade at New London</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Blockade at New London">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After undergoing routine repairs at New York, <i>United States</i> was part of a small squadron that included the newly captured <a href="/wiki/USS_Macedonian_(1810)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Macedonian (1810)">USS&#160;<i>Macedonian</i></a> (formerly HMS <i>Macedonian</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Sloop_of_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Sloop of war">sloop of war</a> <i>Hornet</i>. On May 24, 1813, the squadron departed New York. On that same night <i>United States</i> was struck by lightning which shattered its main mast. By June 1, Decatur's squadron encountered a powerful British squadron on patrol and under the command of <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Hardy,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir Thomas Hardy, 1st Baronet">Sir Thomas Masterman Hardy</a>. Hardy's squadron, which emerged from behind <a href="/wiki/Montauk_Point_State_Park" title="Montauk Point State Park">Montauk Point</a>, consisted of the ships of the line <a href="/wiki/HMS_Ramillies_(1785)" title="HMS Ramillies (1785)">HMS&#160;<i>Ramillies</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Valiant_(1807)" title="HMS Valiant (1807)">HMS&#160;<i>Valiant</i></a> along with the frigates <a href="/wiki/HMS_Acasta_(1797)" title="HMS Acasta (1797)">HMS&#160;<i>Acasta</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/HMS_Orpheus_(1809)" title="HMS Orpheus (1809)">HMS&#160;<i>Orpheus</i></a>. Realizing his only chance for escape was to set a course for <a href="/wiki/New_London,_Connecticut" title="New London, Connecticut">New London</a>, Decatur was forced to flee and take refuge at that port where they were blockaded until the end of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tucker72_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker72-142">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur attempted to sneak out of New London harbor at night in an effort to elude the British blockading squadron.  On the evening of December 18, while attempting to leave the <a href="/wiki/Thames_River_(Connecticut)" title="Thames River (Connecticut)">Thames River</a>, Decatur saw blue lights burning near the mouth of the river in sight of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> blockaders. Decatur was furious, believing that various residents had set the signals to betray his plans. He abandoned the project and returned to New London. In a letter to the Navy Secretary, dated December 20, Decatur charged that traitors in the New London area were in collusion with the British to capture <i>United States</i>, <i>Hornet</i> and <i>Macedonian</i>.  The allegations of <a href="/wiki/Treason" title="Treason">treason</a> soon became public, causing controversy and debate among New London residents and others over the matter. A congressional investigation was called while Decatur made efforts to discover who was responsible but was unsuccessful. Whether the signals were given by a British spy or an American citizen remains uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker72_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker72-142">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Democratic-Republicans (the then-future <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a>) immediately blamed the Federalists who were adamantly against the war from the beginning, and so here earned themselves the name <a href="/wiki/Blue_light_federalists" title="Blue light federalists">"Blue-light Federalists"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Unable to get his squadron out of the harbor, Decatur decided to write a letter to <a href="/wiki/Sir_Thomas_Hardy,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir Thomas Hardy, 1st Baronet">Captain Thomas Hardy</a> offering to negotiate a resolution of the situation at a prearranged meeting.  He proposed that matched ships from either side meet and, in effect, have a duel, to settle their otherwise idle situation. The letter was sent under a <a href="/wiki/White_flag" title="White flag">flag of truce</a> but was in violation of orders, as after the loss of <i>Chesapeake</i>, Navy Secretary Jones forbade commanders from "giving or receiving a Challenge, to or from, an Enemy's vessel."  The next day Hardy gave answer to Decatur's proposal and agreed to have <i>Statira</i> engage <i>Macedonian</i> "as they are sister ships, carrying the same number of guns, and weight of metal." After further deliberation Decatur wanted assurance that <i>Macedonian</i> would not be recaptured should the ship emerge victorious, as he suspected it would be. After several communications it was ascertained that neither side could trust the other and so the proposal floundered, never coming to fruition.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Command_of_USS_President">Command of USS <i>President</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Command of USS President">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_USS_President" title="Capture of USS President">Capture of USS President</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Usspresidentatanchor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Usspresidentatanchor.jpg/300px-Usspresidentatanchor.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Usspresidentatanchor.jpg/450px-Usspresidentatanchor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Usspresidentatanchor.jpg/600px-Usspresidentatanchor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="423" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Usspresidentatanchor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>USS <i>President</i></center></div></div></div>
<p>In May 1814, Decatur transferred his commodore's pennant to <i>President</i>, a frigate with 44 guns.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> By December 1, 1814, Secretary of the Navy <a href="/wiki/William_Jones_(statesman)" title="William Jones (statesman)">William Jones</a>, a staunch proponent of coastal defense, appointed Decatur to lead a four-ship squadron comprising <i>President</i>, which would be the flagship of his new squadron, along with <i>Hornet</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Sloop" title="Sloop">sloop</a> bearing 20 guns, <a href="/wiki/USS_Peacock_(1813)" title="USS Peacock (1813)">USS&#160;<i>Peacock</i></a> bearing 22 and <a href="/wiki/USS_Tom_Bowline_(1814)" title="USS Tom Bowline (1814)">USS&#160;<i>Tom Bowline</i></a> bearing 12 guns. In January 1815, Decatur's squadron was assigned a mission in the <a href="/wiki/East_Indies" title="East Indies">East Indies</a>. However, the British had established a strict blockade in the squadron's port of New York, therefore restricting any cruises.<sup id="cite_ref-Roosevelt_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roosevelt-146">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> On January 14, a severe snowstorm developed, forcing the British squadron away from the coast, but by the next day the storm had subsided, allowing the British fleet to take up positions to the northwest in anticipation of the American fleet trying to escape. The next day <i>President</i> emerged from the west,<sup id="cite_ref-Roosevelt_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roosevelt-146">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> and Decatur attempted to break through the blockade alone in <i>President</i> and make for the appointed rendezvous at <a href="/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Tristan da Cunha">Tristan da Cunha</a>, but encountered the British West Indies Squadron composed of <a href="/wiki/Razee" title="Razee">razee</a> <a href="/wiki/HMS_Majestic_(1785)" title="HMS Majestic (1785)">HMS&#160;<i>Majestic</i></a> bearing 56 guns, under the command of Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Hayes_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="John Hayes (Royal Navy officer)">John Hayes</a>, along with the frigates <a href="/wiki/HMS_Endymion_(1797)" title="HMS Endymion (1797)">HMS&#160;<i>Endymion</i></a>, bearing 40 guns, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hope_(Royal_Navy_officer)" title="Henry Hope (Royal Navy officer)">Captain Henry Hope</a>, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Pomone_(1809)" class="mw-redirect" title="HMS Pomone (1809)">HMS&#160;<i>Pomone</i></a>, bearing 38 guns, commanded by Captain <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Richard_Lumley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Richard Lumley (page does not exist)">John Richard Lumley</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=HMS_Tenedos_(1812)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="HMS Tenedos (1812) (page does not exist)">HMS&#160;<i>Tenedos</i></a>, bearing 38 guns, commanded by Captain <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Parker_(Sea_Lord)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyde Parker (Sea Lord)">Hyde Parker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Decatur had made arrangements for "pilot boats" to mark the way for clear passage out to sea, but due to a plotting error the pilot boats took up the wrong positions and consequently <i>President</i> was accidentally run aground.<sup id="cite_ref-Roosevelt2_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roosevelt2-148">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After an hour upon the sandbar, with Decatur's ship procuring damage to the copper and pintles, the ship finally broke free. Decatur continued the attempt to evade his pursuers and set course along the southerly coast of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>.
</p><p>As <i>Endymion</i> was the fastest ship in the engagement, she was the only ship to catch up to and engage <i>President</i>.  After a fierce fight lasting several hours, during which both ships were severely damaged (<i>Endymion</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s headsails &amp; <i>President</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s hull), Decatur reluctantly surrendered to <i>Endymion</i> as there were four remaining British ships he would have to fight.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Decatur's command suffered 35 men killed and 70 wounded, including Decatur himself who was wounded by a large flying splinter.<sup id="cite_ref-Roosevelt2_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roosevelt2-148">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hickey,_1989,_p.216_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hickey,_1989,_p.216-150">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg/275px-Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg" decoding="async" width="275" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg/413px-Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg/550px-Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg 2x" data-file-width="827" data-file-height="525" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Decatur_by_Davidson.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Decatur lying wounded aboard <i>President</i></div></div></div>
<p><i>Endymion</i> had sustained severe damage to the rigging, and her captain, Hope, decided to carry out repairs before tying up <i>President</i>. While this was happening Decatur made an attempt to escape.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Decatur's frigate was finally overtaken by <i>Pomone</i>. Unaware that Decatur had surrendered, and then tried to flee, <i>Pomone</i> fired two broadsides into <i>President</i> before they realized that the battle was over.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert_149-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> When boats from <i>Pomone</i> boarded <i>President</i> Decatur said "I surrender my sword to the captain of the black ship", a reference to Hope of HMS <i>Endymion</i>. After surrendering a second time, Decatur later claimed, "my ship crippled, and more than a four-fold force opposed to me, without a chance of escape left, I deemed it my duty to surrender." <sup id="cite_ref-Lambert_149-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert-149">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Soon <i>Majestic</i> caught up with the British fleet. Decatur, now dressed in full dress uniform, boarded <i>Majestic</i> and surrendered his sword to Captain Hayes. Hayes in a gesture of admiration returned the sword to Decatur saying that he was "proud in returning the sword of an officer, who had defended his ship so nobly." Before taking possession of <i>President</i>, Hayes allowed Decatur to return to his ship to perform burial services for the officers and seamen who had died in the engagement. He was also allowed to write a letter to his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Decatur along with surviving crew were taken prisoner and held captive in a <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a> prison, arriving January 26, and were held there until February 1815.  Upon arrival at the prison in Bermuda the British naval officers extended various courtesies and provisions that they felt were due to a man of Decatur's stature. The senior naval officer at the prison took the earliest opportunity to parole Decatur to New London, and on February 8, with news of the cessation of hostilities, Decatur traveled aboard <a href="/wiki/HMS_Narcissus_(1801)" title="HMS Narcissus (1801)">HMS&#160;<i>Narcissus</i></a> (32), landing in New London on February 21.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>  On February 26, Decatur arrived in New York City, where he convalesced in a boarding house.
</p><p>At war's end Decatur received a sword as a reward and thanks from Congress for his service in Tripoli and was also awarded the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Gold_Medal" title="Congressional Gold Medal">Congressional Gold Medal</a> for distinguished service in the War of 1812.<sup id="cite_ref-Captain_Stephen_Decatur_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Captain_Stephen_Decatur-153">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Barbary_War">Second Barbary War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Second Barbary War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Barbary_War" title="Second Barbary War">Second Barbary War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg/330px-DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg" decoding="async" width="330" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg/495px-DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg/660px-DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="841" data-file-height="503" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DecaturOffAlgiers.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><center>Decatur's squadron off <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, 1815</center></div></div></div>
<p>Now that war with Britain was over, the United States could concentrate on pressing matters in the Mediterranean, at <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>. As had occurred during the <a href="/wiki/First_Barbary_War" title="First Barbary War">First Barbary War</a> American merchant ships and crews were once again being seized and held for large ransoms. On February 23, 1815, President Madison urged Congress to declare war. Congress approved the act but did not declare war against Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Madison had chosen <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Williams_Crowninshield" title="Benjamin Williams Crowninshield">Benjamin Williams Crowninshield</a> as the new <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="United States Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/William_Jones_(statesman)" title="William Jones (statesman)">William Jones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two squadrons were then assembled, one at New York, under the command of Stephen Decatur, and one at Boston, under the command of Commodore <a href="/wiki/William_Bainbridge" title="William Bainbridge">William Bainbridge</a>. Decatur's squadron of ten ships was ready first and set sail for Algiers on May 20. At this time it was the largest US fleet ever assembled. Decatur was in command of the flagship <a href="/wiki/USS_Guerriere_(1814)" title="USS Guerriere (1814)">USS&#160;<i>Guerriere</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup> Aboard was William Shaler who had just been appointed by Madison as the consul-general for the Barbary States, acting as joint commissioner with Commodores Decatur and Bainbridge.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Shaler was in possession of a letter authorizing them to negotiate terms of peace with the Algerian government.[64] Because of Decatur's great successes in the War of 1812 and for his knowledge of and past experience at the Algerian port, Crowninshield chose him to command the lead ship in the naval squadron to Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_2012_p.9_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_2012_p.9-156">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The US was demanding the release of Americans held captive as slaves, an end of annual payments of tribute, and finally to procure favorable prize agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Decatur was prepared to negotiate peace or resort to military measures. Eager to know the Bey's decision, Decatur dispatched the president's letter which ultimately prompted the Bey to abandon his practice of piracy and kidnapping and come to terms with the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Command_of_USS_Guerriere">Command of USS <i>Guerriere</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Command of USS Guerriere">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On May 20, 1815, Commodore Decatur received instructions from President <a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a> to take command of the frigate <i>Guerriere</i> and lead a squadron of ten ships to the Mediterranean Sea to conduct the <a href="/wiki/Second_Barbary_War" title="Second Barbary War">Second Barbary War</a>, which would put an end to the international practice of paying tribute to the Barbary pirate states. His squadron arrived at <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> on June 14.<sup id="cite_ref-Waldo,_1821_p.248_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waldo,_1821_p.248-162">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before committing himself to the Mediterranean, Decatur learned from the American consuls at <a href="/wiki/Cadiz" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadiz">Cadiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a> of any squadrons passing by along the Atlantic coast or through the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>. To avoid making known the presence of an American squadron, Decatur did not enter the ports but instead dispatched a messenger in a small boat to communicate with the consuls.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>  He learned from observers there that a squadron under the command of the notorious <a href="/wiki/Rais_Hamidou" class="mw-redirect" title="Rais Hamidou">Rais Hamidou</a> had passed by into the Mediterranean, most likely off <a href="/wiki/Cape_Gata" title="Cape Gata">Cape Gata</a>. Decatur's squadron arrived at Gibraltar on June 15, 1815. This attracted much attention and prompted the departure of several dispatch vessels to warn Hammida of the squadron's arrival. Decatur's visit was brief with the consul and lasted only for as long as it took to communicate with a short letter to the Secretary of the Navy informing him of earlier weather problems and that he was about to "proceed in search of the enemy forthwith", where he at once set off in search of Hamidou hoping to take him by surprise.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 17, while sailing in <i>Guerriere</i> for Algiers, Decatur's fleet encountered near <a href="/wiki/Battle_off_Cape_Palos" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle off Cape Palos">Cape Palos</a> the frigate <a href="/wiki/Mashouda" title="Mashouda"><i>Mashouda</i></a>, commanded by Hamidou and the Algerian brig <a href="/w/index.php?title=Estedio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Estedio (page does not exist)"><i>Estedio</i></a>, which were also en route to Algeria. After overtaking the <i>Mashouda</i>, Decatur fired two broadsides, crippling the ship, killing 30 of the crew, including Hamidou himself, and taking more than 400 prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-Waldo,_1821_p.248_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waldo,_1821_p.248-162">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> <i>Lloyd's List</i> reported that the Algerine frigate <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mezoura&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mezoura (page does not exist)"><i>Mezoura</i></a>, which had been under the command of the Algerine admiral, had arrived at <a href="/wiki/Cartagena,_Spain" title="Cartagena, Spain">Carthagena</a> on June 20 as a prize to Decatur's squadron. The newspaper also reported that Decatur's squadron had run another Spanish frigate onshore near Carthagena.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Capturing the <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> of the Algerian fleet at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_off_Cape_Gata" title="Battle off Cape Gata">Battle off Cape Gata</a> Decatur was able to secure sufficient levying power to bargain with the <a href="/wiki/Dey" title="Dey">Dey</a> of Algiers. Upon arrival, Decatur exhibited an early use of <a href="/wiki/Gunboat_diplomacy" title="Gunboat diplomacy">gunboat diplomacy</a> on behalf of American interests as a reminder that this was the only alternative if the Dey decided to decline signing a treaty.  Consequently, a new treaty was agreed upon within 48 hours of Decatur's arrival, confirming the success of his objectives.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After bringing the government in Algiers to terms, Decatur's squadron set sail to <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> to demand reimbursement for proceeds withheld by those governments during the War of 1812. With a similar show of force exhibited at Algiers, Decatur achieved concessions to all of his demands and promptly sailed home victorious. Upon his arrival Decatur boasted to the Secretary of the Navy that the settlement had "been dictated at the mouths of our cannon."<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> For this campaign, he became known as "the Conqueror of the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Pirates" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbary Pirates">Barbary Pirates</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_life">Domestic life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Domestic life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Decatur_house2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Decatur_house2.jpg/260px-Decatur_house2.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Decatur_house2.jpg/390px-Decatur_house2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Decatur_house2.jpg/520px-Decatur_house2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Decatur_house2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stephen Decatur <a href="/wiki/Decatur_House" title="Decatur House">Home</a> in Washington, DC</div></div></div>
<p>After his victory in the Mediterranean over the Barbary states who had terrorized and enslaved Christian merchants for centuries, Decatur returned to the United States, arriving at New York on November 12, 1815, with the brig <i>Enterprise</i>, along with Bainbridge of <i>Guerriere</i> who arrived three days later. He was met with a wide reception from dignitaries and countrymen.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Among the more notable salutations was a letter Decatur received from the Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a> that related the following tidings of appreciation: "I take much interest in informing you that the result of this expedition, so glorious to your country and honorable to yourself and the officers and men under your command, has been very satisfactory to the President."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Secretary of the Navy, <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_W._Crowninshield" title="Benjamin W. Crowninshield">Benjamin W. Crowninshield</a>, was equally gracious and thankful. Since a vacancy was about to occur in the board of Navy commissioners with the retirement of Commodore <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Hull" title="Isaac Hull">Isaac Hull</a>, the Secretary was most anxious to offer the position to Decatur, which he gladly accepted. Upon his appointment Decatur made his journey to Washington, where he was again received with cordial receptions from various dignitaries and countrymen. He served on the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Navy_Commissioners" title="Board of Navy Commissioners">Board of Navy Commissioners</a> from 1816 to 1820. One of his more notable decisions as a commissioner involved his strong objection to the reinstatement of <a href="/wiki/James_Barron" title="James Barron">James Barron</a> upon his return to the United States after being barred from command for five years for <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake%E2%80%93Leopard_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesapeake–Leopard Affair">his questionable handling of the <i>Chesapeake</i></a>, an action that would soon lead to Barron challenging him to a duel.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During his tenure as a Commissioner, Decatur also became active in the Washington social scene. At a social gathering in April 1816, Decatur uttered an after-dinner toast that would become famous:
</p>
<blockquote><p> Our country – in her intercourse with foreign nations, may she always be in the right, and always successful, right or wrong.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> </p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_in_Washington">Home in Washington</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Home in Washington">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_(118102136).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_%28118102136%29.jpg/220px-Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_%28118102136%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_%28118102136%29.jpg/330px-Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_%28118102136%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_%28118102136%29.jpg/440px-Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_%28118102136%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1121" data-file-height="1396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Commodore_Stephen_Decatur_(118102136).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaque outside Decatur's Home</div></div></div>
<p>Now that Decatur was Naval Commissioner he had settled into a routine life in Washington working at the <a href="/wiki/Navy_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Navy Department">Navy Department</a> during the day, with many evenings spent as an honorary guest at social gatherings, as both he and his wife were the toast of Washington society.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_1937_p.174_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_1937_p.174-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Decatur's first home in Washington was 1903 Pennsylvania Avenue (one of the "<a href="/wiki/Seven_Buildings" title="Seven Buildings">Seven Buildings</a>"), purchased in 1817.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In 1818, Decatur built a three-story red brick house in Washington on <a href="/wiki/Lafayette_Square_Historic_District,_Washington,_D.C." title="Lafayette Square Historic District, Washington, D.C.">Lafayette Square</a>, designed by the famous English architect <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Henry_Latrobe" title="Benjamin Henry Latrobe">Benjamin Henry Latrobe</a>, the same man who designed the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Capitol" title="United States Capitol">U.S. Capitol</a> building and <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Episcopal_Church,_Lafayette_Square_(Washington,_D.C.)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Episcopal Church, Lafayette Square (Washington, D.C.)">Saint John's Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Decatur specified that his house had to be suitable for "impressive entertainments". The house was the first private residence to be built near the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>. <a href="/wiki/Decatur_House" title="Decatur House">Decatur House</a> is now a museum that exhibits a large collection of Decatur memorabilia and is managed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Historic_Preservation" title="National Trust for Historic Preservation">National Trust for Historic Preservation</a>. Located on President's Square (<a href="/wiki/President%27s_Park#Lafayette_Park" title="President&#39;s Park">Lafayette Square</a>), it was built in grand style to accommodate large social gatherings, which in the wake of Decatur's many naval victories were an almost routine affair in the lives of Decatur and his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_1937_p.174_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_1937_p.174-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Duel_between_Perry_and_Heath">Duel between Perry and Heath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Duel between Perry and Heath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 1818, at the request of <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hazard_Perry" title="Oliver Hazard Perry">Oliver Hazard Perry</a>, a very close friend, Decatur arrived at New York to act as his second in a <a href="/wiki/Duel" title="Duel">duel</a> between Perry and Captain John Heath, commander of Marines on <a href="/wiki/USS_Java_(1815)" title="USS Java (1815)">USS&#160;<i>Java</i></a>. The two officers were involved in a personal disagreement while aboard that ship, that resulted in Heath challenging Perry to a duel. Perry had written to Decatur nearly a year previously, revealing that he had no intention of firing any shot at Heath. After the two duelists and their seconds assembled the duel took place.  One shot was fired; Heath missed his opponent while Perry, keeping his word, returned no fire. At this point Decatur approached Heath with Perry's letter in hand, relating to Heath that Perry all along had no intention of returning fire and asking Heath if his honor had thus been satisfied. Heath admitted that it had. Decatur was relieved to finally see the matter resolved with no loss of life or limb to either of his friends, urging both to now put the matter behind them.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Barron.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/James_Barron.jpg/200px-James_Barron.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/James_Barron.jpg/300px-James_Barron.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/James_Barron.jpg/400px-James_Barron.jpg 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_Barron.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>James Barron, officer who killed Decatur in a duel, March 22, 1820</div></div></div>
<p>Decatur's life and distinguished service in the U.S. Navy came to an early end when in 1820 when Commodore <a href="/wiki/James_Barron" title="James Barron">James Barron</a> challenged Decatur to a duel, related in part to comments Decatur had made over Barron's conduct in the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake%E2%80%93Leopard_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesapeake–Leopard Affair"><i>Chesapeake</i>–<i>Leopard</i> Affair</a> of 1807. Because of Barron's loss of <i>Chesapeake</i> to the British he faced a court-martial and was barred from command for a term of five years. Decatur had served on the court-martial that had found Barron guilty of "unpreparedness". Barron had just returned to the United States from <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> after being away for six years and was seeking reinstatement.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> He was met with much criticism among fellow naval officers, among whom Decatur was one of the most outspoken. Decatur, who was now on the board of naval commissioners, strongly opposed Barron's reinstatement and was notably critical about the prospect in communications with other naval officers and government officials. As a result, Barron became embittered towards Decatur and challenged him to a duel.<sup id="cite_ref-Toll,_2006_p.470_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toll,_2006_p.470-118">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Barron's challenge to Decatur occurred during a period when duels between officers were so common that it was creating a shortage of experienced men, forcing the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">War Department</a> to threaten to discharge those who attempted to pursue the practice.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Barron's <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/assistant" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:assistant">second</a> was Captain <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Elliott" title="Jesse Elliott">Jesse Elliott</a>, known for his jaunty mannerisms and antagonism toward Decatur. Decatur had first asked his friend <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Macdonough" title="Thomas Macdonough">Thomas Macdonough</a> to be his second, but Macdonough, who had always opposed dueling, accordingly declined his request.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Decatur then turned to his supposed friend Commodore <a href="/wiki/William_Bainbridge" title="William Bainbridge">William Bainbridge</a> to act as his second, to which Bainbridge consented. However, according to naval historian <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Slidell_Mackenzie" title="Alexander Slidell Mackenzie">Alexander Slidell Mackenzie</a>, Decatur made a poor choice: Bainbridge, who was five years his senior, had long been jealous of the younger and more famous Decatur.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The seconds met on March 8 to establish the time and place for the duel and the rules to be followed. The arrangements were exact. The duel was to take place at nine o'clock in the morning on March 22, at <a href="/wiki/Bladensburg_Dueling_Grounds" title="Bladensburg Dueling Grounds">Bladensburg Dueling Grounds</a>, near Washington, at a distance of only eight paces.  Decatur, an expert pistol shot, planned only to wound Barron in the hip.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur did not tell his wife, Susan, about the forthcoming duel but instead wrote to her father asking that he come to Washington to stay with her, using language that suggested that he was facing a duel and that he might lose his life.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> On the morning of the 22nd the dueling party assembled. The conference between the two seconds lasted three-quarters of an hour.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>  Just before the duel, Barron spoke to Decatur of conciliation; however, the men's seconds did not attempt to halt the proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The duel was arranged by Bainbridge with Elliott in a way that made the wounding or death of both duelists very likely. The shooters would be standing close to each other, face to face; there would be no back-to-back pacing away and turning to fire, a procedure that often resulted in the missing of one's opponent. Upon taking their places the duelists were instructed by Bainbridge, "I shall give the word quickly – 'Present, one, two, three' – You are neither to fire before the word 'one', nor after the word 'three'. Now in their positions, each duelist raised his pistol, cocked the flintlock and, while taking aim, stood in silence. Bainbridge called out, 'One' and Decatur and Barron both fired before the count of 'two'. Decatur's shot hit Barron in the lower abdomen and ricocheted into his thigh. Barron's shot hit Decatur in the pelvic area, severing arteries. Both of the duelists fell almost at the same instant. Decatur, mortally wounded and clutching his side, exclaimed, "Oh, Lord, I am a dead man." Lying wounded, Commodore Barron (who ultimately survived) declared that the duel was carried out properly and honorably and told Decatur that he forgave him from the bottom of his heart.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By then other men who had known about the duel were arriving at the scene, including Decatur's friend and mentor, the senior officer <a href="/wiki/John_Rodgers_(1772%E2%80%931838)" title="John Rodgers (1772–1838)">John Rodgers</a>. In excruciating pain, Decatur was carefully lifted by the surgeons and placed in Rodgers' carriage and was carried back to his home on Lafayette Square. Before they departed, Decatur called out to Barron that he should also be taken along, but Rodgers and the surgeons calmly shook their heads in disapproval. Barron cried back "God bless you, Decatur" – and with a weak voice Decatur called back "Farewell, farewell, Barron." Upon arrival at his home, Decatur was taken into the front room just left of the front entrance, still conscious. Before allowing himself to be carried in, he insisted that his wife and nieces be taken upstairs, sparing them the sight of his grave condition.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> A Dr. Thomas Simms arrived from his home nearby to give his assistance to the naval physicians. However, for reasons not entirely clear to historians, Decatur refused to have the ball extracted from his wound.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;i&#93;</a></sup>  At this point Decatur requested that his will be brought forward so as to receive his signature, granting his wife all his worldly possessions, with directives as to who would be the executors of his will.<sup id="cite_ref-Guttridge_p.262_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guttridge_p.262-194">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Decatur died at approximately 10:30&#160;pm that night. While wounded, he is said to have cried out, "I did not know that any man could suffer such pain!"<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Washington society and the nation were shocked upon learning that Decatur had been killed at the age of forty-one in a duel with a rival navy captain. Decatur's funeral was attended by Washington's elite, including President <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe" title="James Monroe">James Monroe</a> and the justices of the Supreme Court, as well as most of Congress. Over 10,000 citizens of Washington and the surrounding area attended to pay their last respects to a national hero. The pallbearers were Commodores Rodgers, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Chauncey" title="Isaac Chauncey">Chauncey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Tingey" title="Thomas Tingey">Tingey</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Porter_(naval_officer)" title="David Porter (naval officer)">Porter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Macdonough" title="Thomas Macdonough">Macdonough</a>; captains Ballard and Cassin; and Lieutenant Macpherson.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Following were naval officers and seamen. At the funeral service a grieving seaman unexpectedly came forward and proclaimed, "He was the friend of the flag, the sailor's friend; the navy has lost its mainmast."<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Stephen Decatur died childless. Though he left his widow $75,000, a fortune at the time, she died virtually penniless in 1850.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Decatur's body was interred in the <a href="/wiki/Joel_Barlow" title="Joel Barlow">Barlow family</a> vault at <a href="/wiki/Kalorama,_Washington,_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Kalorama, Washington, D.C.">Kalorama</a> in accordance with Susan's request. It was later moved to Philadelphia, where he was buried at <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church,_Philadelphia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter&#39;s Church, Philadelphia">St. Peter's Churchyard</a> in 1846, alongside his mother and father.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the funeral, rumors circulated of a last-minute conversation between the duelists that could have avoided the deadly outcome of the duel and, moreover, that the seconds involved might have been planning for such an outcome and accordingly made no real attempts to stop the duel. Decatur's wife Susan held an even more damning view of the matter and spent much of her remaining life pursuing justice for what she termed "the assassins" involved.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Decatur's widow, Susan, tried for several years to obtain a pension from the U.S. Government.  By an act of Congress on March 3, 1837, she was granted a pension retroactive to Decatur's death.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Although he died at a relatively young age, Decatur helped determine the direction of the young nation playing a significant role establishing its identity.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> For his heroism in the Barbary Wars and the War of 1812 Decatur emerged as an icon of American naval history and was roundly admired by most of his contemporaries as well as the citizenry:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Congressional_Gold_Medal_recipients" title="List of Congressional Gold Medal recipients">Congressional Gold Medal</a> awarded January 29, 1813, to honor capture of HMS <i>Macedonian</i> by USS <i>United States</i> under his command.</li>
<li>In honor of Stephen Decatur, five U.S. Navy ships have been named <a href="/wiki/USS_Decatur" title="USS Decatur">USS&#160;<i>Decatur</i></a>.</li>
<li>At the urging of <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, the U.S. Post Office Department issued a series of five stamps honoring the U.S. Navy and various naval heroes, Decatur being one of the few chosen, appearing on the 2-cent issue, along with fellow officer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Macdonough" title="Thomas Macdonough">Macdonough</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>An engraved portrait of Decatur appears on the Series of 1878/1880 $20 <a href="/wiki/Silver_certificate_(United_States)" title="Silver certificate (United States)">silver certificates</a>.</li>
<li>Stephen Decatur's home in Washington, D.C. is a museum owned by the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Historic_Preservation" title="National Trust for Historic Preservation">National Trust for Historic Preservation</a>.</li>
<li>At least 46 communities in the United States have been named after Stephen Decatur, including <a href="/wiki/Decatur,_Alabama" title="Decatur, Alabama">Decatur, Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decatur,_Georgia" title="Decatur, Georgia">Decatur, Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decatur,_Illinois" title="Decatur, Illinois">Decatur, Illinois</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Decatur,_Texas" title="Decatur, Texas">Decatur, Texas</a>.</li>
<li>Seven counties in the United States have been named after Stephen Decatur, including <a href="/wiki/Decatur_County,_Alabama" title="Decatur County, Alabama">Decatur County, Alabama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decatur_County,_Georgia" title="Decatur County, Georgia">Decatur County, Georgia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decatur_County,_Indiana" title="Decatur County, Indiana">Decatur County, Indiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decatur_County,_Iowa" title="Decatur County, Iowa">Decatur County, Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Decatur_County,_Kansas" title="Decatur County, Kansas">Decatur County, Kansas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Decatur_County,_Tennessee" title="Decatur County, Tennessee">Decatur County, Tennessee</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a> county named for Steven Decatur has its county seat at <a href="/wiki/Bainbridge,_Georgia" title="Bainbridge, Georgia">Bainbridge</a>.</li>
<li>In honor to Stephen Decatur, the Borough of <a href="/wiki/Doylestown,_Pennsylvania" title="Doylestown, Pennsylvania">Doylestown, Pennsylvania</a>, incorporated a street in his name.</li>
<li>Decatur Avenue in <a href="/wiki/Norman,_Oklahoma" title="Norman, Oklahoma">Norman, Oklahoma</a>, is named in honor of Decatur, as is <a href="/wiki/Decatur_Boulevard" title="Decatur Boulevard">Decatur Boulevard</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, Decatur Street in Mineral Point, Wisconsin and Decatur Avenue in Minneapolis, Minnesota.</li>
<li>In honor of Stephen Decatur, in the county of Worcester, Maryland, where he was born, a street, monument, park, and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur_Middle_School_(Berlin)" title="Stephen Decatur Middle School (Berlin)">middle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur_High_School_(Maryland)" title="Stephen Decatur High School (Maryland)">high schools</a> are named after him. His birthplace is marked in the current town of Berlin, Maryland.</li>
<li>A main <a href="/wiki/Decatur_Street_(New_Orleans)" title="Decatur Street (New Orleans)">thoroughfare in New Orleans' French Quarter</a> is named Decatur in his honor.</li>
<li>An island in the San Juan Archipelago (Washington state) is named Decatur Island</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Decatur_Township,_Michigan" title="Decatur Township, Michigan">Decatur Township</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_County,_Michigan" title="Van Buren County, Michigan">Van Buren County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a> is named in his honor.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<table>
<tbody><tr>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Other notable naval commanders of the time:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Jones" title="John Paul Jones">John Paul Jones</a></li>
<li>Commodore <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">John Barry</a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Stephen_Decatur&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Town was destroyed by hurricane in 1818, rebuilt years later and named <a href="/wiki/Berlin,_Maryland" title="Berlin, Maryland">'Berlin'</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some sources spell the name as <i>Siren</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis,_1937_p.43_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis,_1937_p.43-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-71">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Whipple, 2001 claims only two gunboats were offered.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some sources claim the man could have been <a href="/wiki/Ruben_James" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruben James">Ruben James</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Striking colors, i.e.Lowering the ship's flag, was an international signal of surrender. </span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-131"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-131">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Monroe was later <a href="/wiki/James_Monroe#Secretary_of_State_and_Secretary_of_War" title="James Monroe">appointed Secretary of War</a> in September 1814.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The ten vessels were:<br />Frigates: USS <i>Guerrier</i> (flagship), USS <i>Macedonian</i> and USS <i>Constellation</i>;<br />sloop of war <a href="/wiki/USS_Ontario_(1813)" title="USS Ontario (1813)">USS&#160;<i>Ontario</i></a>; brigs <a href="/wiki/USS_Epervier_(1814)" class="mw-redirect" title="USS Epervier (1814)">USS&#160;<i>Epervier</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Firefly_(1814)" title="USS Firefly (1814)">USS&#160;<i>Firefly</i></a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=USS_Flambeau_(1814)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="USS Flambeau (1814) (page does not exist)">USS&#160;<i>Flambeau</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Spark_(1813)" title="USS Spark (1813)">USS&#160;<i>Spark</i></a>;<br />schooners <a href="/wiki/USS_Spitfire_(1814)" title="USS Spitfire (1814)">USS&#160;<i>Spitfire</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/USS_Torch_(1814)" title="USS Torch (1814)">USS&#160;<i>Torch</i></a>.<br />Three of these vessels were prizes taken in the War of 1812.<sup id="cite_ref-Tucker,_2012_p.9_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tucker,_2012_p.9-156">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-176"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-176">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The toast is more widely known in the form of a paraphrase that arose decades later (e.g. <a href="#Mackenzie">Mackenzie, 1846</a>, p. 443) with "but right or wrong, our country" instead of the original "and always successful, right or wrong".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-195"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-195">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Among the current sources only Guttridge mentions Decatur's refusal to have the ball extracted, not citing any reason.<sup id="cite_ref-Guttridge_p.262_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guttridge_p.262-194">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
